## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task seeks a constitutive relationship σ(ε, T) describing stress as a function of strain and temperature, which is fundamental in materials science and solid mechanics. Temperature typically causes thermal softening (reducing stiffness and flow stress), while strain governs elastic and plastic deformation behavior.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear plastic stress-strain, Hollomon equation)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (combined strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Arrhenius-type thermal factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (exponential thermal softening)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress offset)
- Ludwik with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T) (Ludwik with Arrhenius thermal factor)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power law for pre-strained material)
- Swift with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (Swift + Johnson-Cook thermal term)
- Polynomial with temperature: sigma = (c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2) * (c2 + c3 * T) (quadratic strain with linear T dependence)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**(-1) (softening at large strain)
- Hyperbolic sine flow stress: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Sellars-Tegart / Garofalo model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear thermal softening → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (Tm - T) indicating modulus or strength decreasing linearly with temperature
- Exponential thermal softening → Factor exp(-c*T) representing Arrhenius-type thermally activated processes
- Strain hardening saturation → Forms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicating stress approaching a plateau at large strains
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 representing diminishing hardening rate (work hardening)
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant (c0 + f(epsilon)) representing initial yield strength before plastic hardening begins
- Homologous temperature scaling → T appears as ratio or shifted form (c1 - T) or (Tm - T)/(Tm - Tref) for normalized thermal effects
- Multiplicative separability → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) indicating strain and temperature effects are decoupled/separable
- Shifted strain origin → (epsilon + c)**n instead of epsilon**n to account for pre-existing strain or avoid singularity at zero strain

GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci22)

GT: c0*epsilon**c1 + epsilon*c2*sin(T - c3)
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT:** `72.331*epsilon**2 + epsilon*7.747*sin(T - 287.774)`

Using the identity: `sin(T - c3) = sin(T)cos(c3) - cos(T)sin(c3)`, so:
`epsilon*7.747*sin(T - 287.774) = epsilon*7.747*cos(287.774)*sin(T) - epsilon*7.747*sin(287.774)*cos(T)`

Let me compute: cos(287.774) and sin(287.774). Since 287.774 ≈ 287.774 radians... but this is in radians. Let me compute mod 2π: 287.774/(2π) ≈ 45.8, so 287.774 - 45*2π ≈ 287.774 - 282.743 ≈ 5.031 radians.

cos(5.031) ≈ 0.3178, sin(5.031) ≈ -0.9482

So the sin/cos decomposition: `epsilon*7.747*0.3178*sin(T) + epsilon*7.747*0.9482*cos(T)` = `epsilon*2.462*sin(T) + epsilon*7.345*cos(T)`

The GT is: `72.331*epsilon**2 + 2.462*epsilon*sin(T) + 7.345*epsilon*cos(T)`

Now I need `epsilon*sin(T)` terms too. Many candidates only have `epsilon*cos(T)` but not `epsilon*sin(T)`.

**Candidate 8:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon*cos(T) + c5*epsilon**5*sin(T*c6 + c7)`

Setting c0=0 (kills T*epsilon), c1=0, c3=2 gives c2*epsilon**2, c4*epsilon*cos(T). But we need epsilon*sin(T) — could get it from c5*epsilon**5*sin(T*c6+c7) only if epsilon**5 becomes epsilon, which requires specific epsilon values, not for all epsilon. No match.

**Candidate 37:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1 + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon*cos(T)` — only has epsilon*cos(T), missing epsilon*sin(T). No.

**Candidate 42:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1 + c2*epsilon*cos(T) + c3*epsilon*sin(T*c4 + c5) + c6*epsilon`

Set c0=0, c4=1: `c1 + c2*epsilon*cos(T) + c3*epsilon*sin(T + c5) + c6*epsilon`

Expand: `c3*epsilon*sin(T+c5) = c3*epsilon*(sin(T)cos(c5) + cos(T)sin(c5))`

So total cos(T) coefficient: `(c2 + c3*sin(c5))*epsilon`, sin(T) coefficient: `c3*cos(c5)*epsilon`, plus `c6*epsilon + c1`.

We need: c1=0, c6*epsilon = 72.331*epsilon**2. But c6*epsilon is linear in epsilon, not quadratic. No match.

**Candidate 26:** `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + c2 + c3*epsilon*cos(T) + c4*epsilon*sin(T*c5 + c6)`

Set c0=0, c1=0, c5=1: `c2 + c3*epsilon*cos(T) + c4*epsilon*sin(T + c6)`. Same problem — no epsilon**2 term.

**Candidate 15:** `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + c2*epsilon + c3 + c4*epsilon*cos(T) + c5*epsilon**c6*sin(T*c7 + c8)`

Hmm, none of the candidates seem to match. Let me reconsider whether I'm being too restrictive. Let me re-examine the GT:

GT = c0*epsilon^c1 + epsilon*c2*sin(T - c3) with c3 ≈ 287.77

Note that c3 ≈ 287.77 ≈ 91.5*π ≈ 287.77. Actually 91π ≈ 285.88, 92π ≈ 289.03. So c3 is not a nice multiple of π.

sin(T - 287.77) — this is just sin(T + phase). The key point is that the GT requires:
1. epsilon² term
2. epsilon*sin(T + phase) term (which decomposes to epsilon*sin(T) and epsilon*cos(T))

Let me reconsider candidates that have epsilon*sin(T+phase) explicitly.

The last term c5*epsilon^5*sin(T*c6+c7) — if c5=0, we lose it. Then we have epsilon² + epsilon*cos(T) but no epsilon*sin(T).

What if I DON'T set c5=0? Then I have an extra epsilon^5*sin(T+c7) term that doesn't appear in GT. Can't zero it without setting c5=0.

So indeed, none of these candidates can produce all three required basis functions {epsilon², epsilon*sin(T), epsilon*cos(T)}.

We can't have both. So Candidate 15 still doesn't work.

Actually, wait. Let me reconsider. What if we use c6=1, c7=1 to get epsilon*sin(T+c8), and then use c2*epsilon... but c2*epsilon can't become epsilon².
